				<script type="text/javascript">
			$J( function() {
				BindAutoFlyoutEvents();

				var $Window = $J(window);
				var $Header = $J('#store_header');
				var $ResponsiveNavWindowShadeCtn = $J('#responsive_store_nav_ctn');
				var $ResponsiveNavOverlay = $J('#responsive_store_nav_overlay');
				var $ResponsiveNavOverlayCtn = $J('#responsive_store_nav_overlay_ctn');
				var $ResponsiveNavOverlayBottom = $J('#responsive_store_nav_overlay_bottom');
				var $HeaderWrapper;
				$Window.on('Responsive_SmallScreenModeToggled.StoreMenu', function() {
					var bUseSmallScreenMode = window.UseSmallScreenMode && window.UseSmallScreenMode();

											if ( !$HeaderWrapper )
							$HeaderWrapper = $Header.wrap( $J('<div/>', {'class': 'responsive_store_nav_ctn_spacer'} ) ).parent();

						if ( bUseSmallScreenMode )
							$ResponsiveNavWindowShadeCtn.append( $Header );
						else
							$HeaderWrapper.append( $Header );


						if ( bUseSmallScreenMode )
						{
							$Header.css( 'visibility', 'hidden' );
							$Header.show();

							var nStartingScrollPosition = $J('#store_header').height();
							if ( $Window.scrollTop() < nStartingScrollPosition )
								$Window.scrollTop( nStartingScrollPosition );

							$Header.css('visibility', 'visible');
						}
									} );
				
				window.setTimeout( function() { $J(window).trigger('Responsive_SmallScreenModeToggled.StoreMenu'); }, 0 );

										var g_rgUserPreferences = {
							excluded_tags : [],
							excluded_content_descriptors : [3,4]						};
						
													g_rgUserPreferences['use_store_query'] = 1;
						
						g_rgUserPreferences['use_search_spellcheck'] = 1;
						g_rgUserPreferences['search_creators_and_tags'] = 1;

						if( $J('#searchform').length > 0 )
						{
							// default search support where the web page includes the search edit control
							EnableSearchSuggestions( $J('#searchform')[0].elements['term'], '1_5_9_', 'SG', 1, 'schinese', g_rgUserPreferences, '20235278' );
						}
						else 
						{
							// search support for the mobile client.  the mobile client has a native search edit control but relies on the web content to perform the query and show results
													}
				
				// make genre categories expand/collapse on mobile
				$J(document).on( 'click', '.popup_genre_expand_header', function ( event ) {
					if ( !UseSmallScreenMode() )
						return;

					event.preventDefault();
					var $Element = $J(this);
					var $Target = $J('.popup_genre_expand_content[data-genre-group=' + $Element.data('genre-group') + ']' );
					if ( $Element.data('group-expanded') )
					{
						$Target.slideUp();
						$Element.data( 'group-expanded', false );
					}
					else
					{
						$Target.slideDown();
						$Element.data( 'group-expanded', true );
					}
				});
			} );
		</script>

												<img class="movie_thumb" src="https://cdn.akamai.steamstatic.com/steam/apps/256751617/movie.184x123.jpg?t=1559062853">
												<div class="highlight_movie_marker"></div>
											</div>
											                                    </div>
                                </div>
                                                                    <div class="slider_ctn">
                                        <div id="highlight_slider_left" class="slider_left"><span></span></div>
                                        <div class="slider" id="highlight_slider">
                                            <div class="slider_bg">
                                            </div>
                                            <div class="handle" style="position: absolute; left: 0px;">
                                            </div>
                                        </div>
                                        <div id="highlight_slider_right" class="slider_right"><span></span></div>
                                    </div>
                                    <script type="text/javascript">
                                        $J( function() {
                                            var player = new HighlightPlayer( {
                                                elemPlayerArea: 'highlight_player_area',
                                                elemStrip: 'highlight_strip',
                                                elemStripScroll: 'highlight_strip_scroll',
                                                elemSlider: 'highlight_slider',
                                                rgScreenshotURLs: rgScreenshotURLs
                                            } );

                                            $J('#highlight_slider_right').click( function() {
                                                player.Transition( true );
                                            });
                                            $J('#highlight_slider_left').click( function() {
                                                player.TransitionBack( true );
                                            });

                                            
                                                // swipe gesture handling for the media carousel

                                                // TODO: We may want to move all of this to the player class so it has built in touch gesture support.
                                                // First testing here as part of new mobile ux.

                                                var k_nElementWidth = 120;
                                                var k_playerItemClassName = '.highlight_player_item';
                                                var g_nStripWidth = 3240;
                                                var g_nMediaItems = player.m_elemPlayerArea.find( '.highlight_player_item' ).length;
                                                var g_TouchEventStart = null;

                                                // Handle left/right swipe on the media playback by moving forward or backward when the swipe completes
                                                $J('#highlight_player_area').on("touchstart", function (event) {
                                                    g_TouchEventStart = event;
                                                });
                                                $J('#highlight_player_area').on("touchmove", function (event) {

                                                    if ( typeof g_TouchEventStart == undefined )
                                                        return;

                                                    var xdiff = Math.abs( g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX - event.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX );
                                                    var ydiff = Math.abs( g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY - event.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY );

                                                    // To reduce unintended page scroll during a horizontal swipe block the default handler when it looks like the user
                                                    // is in the process of performaing a horizontal scroll
                                                    if ( xdiff > ydiff && ( typeof event.cancelable !== 'boolean' || event.cancelable ) )
                                                        event.preventDefault();

                                                });
                                                $J('#highlight_player_area').on("touchend", function (eventEnd) {

                                                    if ( typeof g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0] == undefined ||
                                                        typeof eventEnd.originalEvent.changedTouches[0] == undefined )
                                                        return;

                                                    var xdiff = g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX - eventEnd.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX;
                                                    var ydiff = g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY - eventEnd.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY;

                                                    // clear out the touch start event
                                                    g_TouchEventStart = null;

                                                    // ignore the swipe if it was short and could've been intended as a tap, or the
                                                    // direction was more vertical than horizontal
                                                    if ( Math.abs( xdiff ) < 20 || Math.abs( ydiff ) > Math.abs( xdiff ) )
                                                        return;

                                                    // we're handling this event
                                                    if ( typeof event.cancelable !== 'boolean' || event.cancelable )
                                                        event.preventDefault();

                                                    // move forward or backward but don't wrap as that would be a jarring user experience
                                                    if ( xdiff > 0 )
                                                    {
                                                        var $NextItem = player.m_activeItem.next( k_playerItemClassName );
                                                        if ( $NextItem.length )
                                                            player.Transition( true );
                                                    }
                                                    else
                                                    {
                                                        var $NextItem = player.m_activeItem.prev( k_playerItemClassName );
                                                        if ( $NextItem.length )
                                                            player.TransitionBack( true );
                                                    }
                                                });

                                                // when the thumbnail strip is swiped move the strip at a granular level
                                                // so it feels active.  The active image does not update because when testing the code to
                                                // make it change the active element it seemed annoying
                                                var g_nSwipeStartingPosition = 0;
                                                var g_nMaxScroll = g_nMediaItems > 3 ? ( ( g_nMediaItems - 3 ) * k_nElementWidth ) : 0;

                                                $J('#highlight_strip_scroll').on("touchstart", function (event) {
                                                    g_TouchEventStart = event;
                                                    g_nSwipeStartingPosition = parseInt( player.m_elemStripScroll.css( 'left' ) );

                                                    player.StopCycle();
                                                });
                                                $J('#highlight_strip_scroll').on("touchmove", function (event) {

                                                    if ( typeof g_TouchEventStart == undefined )
                                                        return;

                                                    // To reduce unintended page scroll during a horizontal swipe block the default handler when it looks like the user
                                                    // is in the process of performaing a horizontal scroll
                                                    var xdiff = parseInt( event.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX - g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenX );
                                                    var ydiff = parseInt( event.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY - g_TouchEventStart.originalEvent.changedTouches[0].screenY );
                                                    if ( Math.abs(ydiff) > Math.abs(xdiff) )
                                                        return;

                                                    // move the scroll strip without changing the selected item
                                                    var nNewScrollPosition = parseInt( g_nSwipeStartingPosition + xdiff );

                                                    // check that we don't scroll past the ends
                                                    if ( nNewScrollPosition > 0 )
                                                        nNewScrollPosition = 0;
                                                    else if ( nNewScrollPosition < (-1 * g_nMaxScroll) )
                                                        nNewScrollPosition = (-1 * g_nMaxScroll);

                                                    // set the new scroll position
                                                    player.m_elemStripScroll.css( 'left', nNewScrollPosition + 'px' );

                                                    // we're handling this event
                                                    if ( typeof event.cancelable !== 'boolean' || event.cancelable )
                                                        event.preventDefault();
                                                });
                                                $J('#highlight_strip_scroll').on("touchend", function (eventEnd) {
                                                    g_TouchEventStart = null;
                                                    g_nSwipeStartingPosition = 0;
                                                });

										
                                            if( window.location.hash )
                                            {
                                                var ssid = window.location.hash.substr(1);
                                                player.HighlightScreenshot(ssid);
                                            }
                                        } );
                                    </script>
                                                            </div>
                        					</div>
				</div>
				<div style="clear: both;"></div>
			</div>
			</div>

2 V1.5 Physics Development Update","posttime":1690305062,"updatetime":1690307522,"body":"Greetings Everyone!\n\nAutomobilista 2 V1.5 is finally just around the corner! The weeks since our last catch-up have been intense, with every front of development pushing flat-out to make this milestone update as great as we all hoped it would be. As a result, the time for producing and writing these dev updates got significantly reduced as we focused on the main job at hand, but things are finally far along enough that we can take the time to share some more info with you about the new update just in time for its official release! \n\nAmong the many highlights of AMS2 V1.5, the most eagerly awaited is likely to be the major physics overhaul we first discussed on a Dev Update earlier this year, and of which users already had a taste for with some selected classes in v1.4.8.\n\nThis article aims to give a brief overview over the physics development methodology of AMS2 for this update and generally as we move on to additional content, as well as shed a little more light into the scope of the V1.5 physics developments as well as what triggered this overhaul. Buckle up as we go technical!\n\n[h3]Car Physics Development[\/h3]\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/90391d4791041804a22eca98fc1ff8ab74342012.jpg[\/img]\n\nNot long after V1.4 release last year (itself a major milestone with critical developments to tire thermodynamics and driveline which carry over and complement the work done for V1.5) we discovered a bug in the pMotor \/ SETA interaction that caused tire carcass spring \/ damper rates to behave inconsistently from what we are setting them to be, which has repercussions in the car\u00b4s suspension and aerodynamics. In isolation, fixing this bug would not have been hugely consequential for cars that aren\u00b4t heavily aerodynamical, but it has been the critical foundational step for all other developments that followed, and which now add up to a truly momentous step-up in accuracy for any and all types of cars.\n\nEvery physics front - chassis, aerodynamics, suspension, driveline, engine, brakes and obviously tires for each of the 272 physics variants in the game have been at minimum double-checked, and at maximum completely rewritten: suspension geometries are considerably more accurate to the model simulated; spring and damper rates (critical to tires and aerodynamics) exhaustively revised, differentials fine-tuned, engine torque curves adjusted, and new car-specific systems and functionalities such as frontal DRS for the Sigma P1 G5 and Metalmoro AJR Gen2 or e-diff systems for the Mclaren 570 GT4 or the VW TSI Cup cars implemented; the force feedback for each of the variants has in turn been carefully fine-tuned for each car\u00b4s characteristics for a much more detailed feel for the revamped tire and suspension physics.\n\nThe whole physics development process both for creating new cars as well as revising existing cars begins with extensive data collection on the vehicle at hand - sometimes manufacturers will provide us with all we could need, and sometimes it\u00b4s on us to go on the hunt to scramble the required info from various sources - once we have collected at least the basic specs and dimensions (mass, engine output, gear ratios, positions of aero devices, wheelbase, track width), a baseline is created on top of an existing similar car (or the \"old\" car if it\u00b4s a revision instead of a new car), applying those basic specs to it.\n\n[b]Pictured Below: [\/b]Thorough Factory Setup sheet for Ginetta G58\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/ec4d167b2c44c2db9052dbfad1a9dc064e3d97a9.png[\/img]\n\nThe chassis then gets its undertray and collision mesh defined - this is important not only for defining the car\u00b4s \"hit box\" against walls and other cars, but also to set up the floor coordinates which is the reference plane from which many physics calculations are drawn from. The floor position and angle also affects how the car reacts when bottoming out or scrapping over curbs.\n\n[b]Pictured below: [\/b]Formula Dirt collision mesh\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/784b34ca271b348aba96d3e762b93c4b053ead8e.jpg[\/img]\nOnce that is done, we move on to the modelling of the suspension geometry - for modern cars, it is not unusual for developers to be supplied with a detailed CAD model of the car, from which we can export coordinates of suspension arms, axles and rods to create a 1:1 representation of the real thing.\n\n[b]Pictured below:[\/b] The suspension geometry of a P1 prototype as provided by its constructor.\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/f6280132d43f076b4bd802345ba8d1af14f4c907.jpg[\/img]\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/a7dbe4d0481511e6f7c41ee8d0b49fe34a178040.jpg[\/img]\n\nFor historical machines we unfortunately seldom have the privileges of CAD models and data recording, and in such cases research is critical as quality pictures can allow us to get results that are just as accurate as those modelled from CAD data.\n\n[b]Pictured Below:[\/b] Mclaren M23 suspension geometry plotted from a real picture.\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/18329c6ea38b250703af5efe8f62885ca4450ac6.jpg[\/img]\n\n[b]Pictured Below: [\/b]Suspension Geometry as modelled in the Mclaren MP4\/6\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/31417d4b6019993338f9bdb6b789ddc38a0d4321.jpg[\/img]\nOnce the geometry is modelled, we move on to working out suspension wheel rates, heave frequencies and establishing critical damping ratios which we do with the aid of an internally developed suspension physics calculator as pictured below.\n\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/75db941852ba2ab4ad9e3a0ff786240fbe8d0ce1.png[\/img]\nIt is then time to take the virtual car out on track for a virtual shakedown and to lay down its tire carcass framework, adjusting deflection as well as longitudinal, lateral and sidewall properties to make sure the tire is within expected flex and stretch limits; testing on a diverse number of tracks subjecting tires through trail braking, bumps, undulations, curbs, on and off-camber turns at various speeds allows for adjusting spring\/damping\/carcass adjustments to something more adequate for the car.\n\n[previewyoutube=V9pLXdjXTZ8;full][\/previewyoutube]\n\n[b]Pictured below:[\/b] STM carcass \"network\" showing flex control points and their relationship with one another.\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/b8329708cf219cbbddd3b6127f682c845c642105.png[\/img]\nThe focus is then shifted to revising tire treads and aerodynamics over which a lot of the performance and handling of the cars is defined, adjusting all friction, lift and drag coefficients to match as well as possible the real car data we have gathered.\n\n[u]Pictured below:[\/u] Live spectral analysis of longitudinal tread \"stretching\" (y axis) and lateral tread flex (x axis). Top left = Front Left; Top right = Front Right; Bottom left = Rear left; Bottom Right = Rear right.\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/7a29d8de719ec81eccee2b3fea78f30d50cedd97.png[\/img]\n\nThe tire carcass and suspension along with the loads they get subjected to affect the cars\u00b4 ride heights, which in turn carries significant impact on the car\u00b4s aerodynamics, and that in turn impacts the loads on the carcass and suspension - from this point onwards thus the work fine-tuning all fronts need to progress somewhat concurrently to ensure all components are working in harmony.\n\n[b]Pictured below: [\/b]Tire traction circle analysis to gauge lateral \/ longitudinal forces the tire is being subjected to\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/408f7de9d538e148c4b1ce017778e10c856c6d45.png[\/img]\n\n[b]Pictured below: [\/b]Bias ply carcass from a Lotus 49C tire gets bent out of shape under hard cornering load [img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/8e5ebeea18c349d3c306fd066b5e47384452e384.jpg[\/img]\n\nOnce things are far along enough, focus is shifted to the driveline - engine, clutch, gearbox, differential, drive shafts and even wheel bearings properties are modelled and should be to properly fine-tuned to ensure the power delivery to the wheel is realistically reproduced. A relevant v1.5 development to cite is in how differential locking torque could briefly become too low during braking zones, trail braking and sustained throttle, under which circumstances the reduced torque applied to the differential ramps could upset the driven axle causing the car to possibly feel unstable or unpredictable. Thanks to a physics logic improvement and diff setups in revised cars there is steady locking torque in these same circumstances, which makes the differential more predictable especially with higher preloads.\n\n[b]Pictured Below:[\/b] Wheel Slip Graph\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/ce7fa1fe81b712fd02a7711bbe5fd635aee8fe87.png[\/img]\n\nThere is much more to physics development than what\u00b4s covered above - we haven\u00b4t touched wear & tear of components, AMDM nor gone in-depth the aero and chassis side in the overview above, but this should give everyone an idea of what this whole process entails.\n\n[h3]V1.5 Surface Physics Development[\/h3]\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/9e0a6ed238aaa8002e4691dff345ab03661277f7.jpg[\/img]\n\nAMS2 V1.5 also brings substantial progress to the front of surface physics, not least due to the introduction of dirt \/ rallycross raising requiring attention to be given to modelling of deformable terrains and the way cars and tires interact with it, picking up and then laying down the dirt around the non-dirt segments of the race track. While LiveTrack does a lot of the heavy-lifting there for us, its properties still need to be adjusted and verified for optimal results.\n[img]{STEAM_CLAN_IMAGE}\/35138208\/1d1ea982e8fa98f43b1e647cad3f7962c1618dcd.jpg[\/img]\n\nThese in turn triggered several other LiveTrack developments which will be introduced as of V1.5 release. To begin with, the grip range going from a \"green\" track to a fully rubbered one has been extended, so a green track is a bit lower grip than before and it carries on until heavy rubber at which point grip is the same as it used to be. Track rubber state thus has a bigger impact in handling and performance. Do note however that a rubbered racing line tends to shift car balance to understeer - you may want to adjust your setup to make the best of the extra grip.\n\nRubber dynamics are also now flipped during rainy weather - in AMS2 V1.5 water saturation leads to rubber becoming more slippery than non-rubbered parts of the track, which in turn means the normal racing line should be avoided when wet as it\u00b4s actually lower grip, just like it is in real life. The curbs are likewise also now more slippery when wet and shouldn\u00b4t be abused especially if slick tires are still in use.\n\n[h3]The Reiza Physics Development Team[\/h3]\n\nAll these developments add up to a driving experience that is unlike anything else in sim racing at the moment, and the relentless push that has led to so much progress over the course of AMS2 development as we went through one exhaustive (and exhausting) revamp after another seemingly in constant loop could only have come to fruition at the hands of a highly talented, driven team - besides (and much more importantly than) myself supervising the overall process and making some contributions in my areas of expertise, we have:\n\n@Domagoj Lovric at the center of it from the very beginning, doing critical work digging through the code to figure out how things worked in this engine, and more importantly debugging and fixing it when it didn\u00b4t; Dom also developed a new FFB system from the ground up and constantly refined it along with the default FFB profiles, all the while pushing to make it easier for users to create and share their own;\n\n@oez joined us in the second year of AMS2 release, going from just a tech-savvy user of the sim to a hands-on developer - although he has since moved on to another game studio, his contributions firstly fixing a major bug in the driveline physics, then adjusting drivelines for each car specifications, as well as developing AMDM remain critical to AMS2 physics status as it is today;\n\n@steelreserv likewise made the jump from user working on car setups to developer putting together core physics components, creating along the way the physics calculator shown above that has been so important for setting up solid foundations for all cars in the game and probably making Tom the one in the team with the stronger grasp on the inner workings of the SETA Tire Model;\n\nHelping him along in that process is @Gringo who in recent months added car physics to his job description to go along with the track development he\u00b4s been doing for us for many years now, making some important discoveries and handling most of the suspension geometry revisions described further up this article;\n\n@CrimsonEminence, also was originally a hardcore user who would constantly (but constructively) push us with persisting physics feedback and who today makes his own direct contributions to it, helping with tire thermodynamics and developing default setups along with extensive testing, keeping us all honest (many times by redirecting forum feedback) when something does not appear to be working as it should;\n\nFinally @Coanda who first gets the ball rolling with invaluable in-depth research on each car and class we have modelled in the sim, and then brings them home with meticulous FFB fine-tuning & customization for each car to convey all the details from these tire & suspension revisions;\n\nThroigh it all, we have continued to draw from the deep wells of consultancy knowledge as well as the formidable foundation set primarily by @Niels Heusinkveld in AMS1 cars, which remain largely in use in their AMS2 counterparts.\n\nTake just one of these skilled and highly dedicated people and their contributions out of the equation and we certainly wouldn\u00b4t be where we are now on this rundown for v1.5 release - the combination of their dedication with the capabilities of the Madness Physics engine have gradually added up to a potent whole that is even greater than the sum of the parts, and with v1.5 we take a decisive step towards bringing it all together.\n\nWe are really looking forward to sharing the results with you, and hope you enjoy driving it as much as we do!\n","commentcount":53,"tags":["mod_reviewed","ModAct_441547739_1690306302_0"],"language":0,"hidden":0,"forum_topic_id":"3800526046843571441","event_gid":"3648529365556084889","voteupcount":830,"votedowncount":6,"ban_check_result":0,"banned":0},"published":1,"hidden":0,"rtime32_visibility_start":1690305060,"rtime32_visibility_end":0,"broadcaster_accountid":0,"follower_count":0,"ignore_count":0,"forum_topic_id":"3800526046843571441","rtime32_last_modified":1694238348,"news_post_gid":"0","rtime_mod_reviewed":1690306302,"featured_app_tagid":0,"referenced_appids":[],"build_id":0,"build_branch":"","votes_up":830,"votes_down":6,"comment_type":"ForumTopic","gidfeature":"1633040337746026530","gidfeature2":"3800526046843571441"},{"gid":"3648531811782467738","clan_steamid":"103582791464659616","event_name":"Automobilista 						<div id="game_area_description" class="game_area_description">
							<h2>关于这款游戏</h2>
							Automobilista 2 is a celebration of motorsports - a comprehensive simulator powered by genre-leading technology placing you right at the center of the thrills the sport has provided over the decades, with an uniquely immersive experience and unmatched variety of cars, tracks and features you won´t find in any other racing game; it is an advanced simulator that never forgets to remain fun and accessible.<br><br>Within a few clicks, you can jump from a rental kart for modern day race in downtown Sao Paulo to a historic Grand Prix car for a blast around Monzas famous banking as if it were the 1960s; Run one of the championship seasons offered within the game, or create your own custom season setting up classes, tracks, points system, weather to your preference;; Travel through the history of motorsports driving legendary machines such as the Lotus 72E, the mighty Group C Porsche 962c or the Mclaren F1 GTR on the tracks they actually belonged; enjoy the unique driving experiences of exotic race cars equipped with ingenious devices that made motorsports folklore never before modeled in a racing simulator, such as the Brabham BT46B fan car or the Mclaren MP4-12 with its ingenuous brake steer system; explore the freedom that Automobilista 2 provides to create great events that never were, or even really crazy ones that never could be.<br><br>There is more still to come in the years ahead - new cars &amp; tracks, more historical content, different racing modes, enhanced gameplay features, better racing for both single and multiplayer; AMS2 continues to be an ever-evolving, ever-expanding project that will continue to get bigger and better.<h2 class="bb_tag">RACE ANYTHING, ANYWHERE, ANYHOW</h2>From rental Karts to high-performance Prototypes, Classic Grand Prix cars to modern GTs and Racing Trucks, Automobilista 2 offers it all through a catalogue of beautifully-detailed venues across five continents.<h2 class="bb_tag">ACCESSIBLE VISUAL REALISM</h2>Automobilista 2 combines world-class graphics with optimized performance to offer glorious visuals even on less powerful systems, and one of the best VR experiences of any racing game<h2 class="bb_tag">FULLY DYNAMIC RACING</h2>Featuring the most advanced dynamic weather and track condition systems, 24-hour cycles, barometric pressure modelling, varying wind speeds and temperatures — all to produce ever-changing conditions session to session. AMS2 gives you full control for races to progress just as you want it, ensuring no two laps are the same<h2 class="bb_tag">REAL WEATHER</h2> - Real Weather links AMS2´s ultra-advanced weather system with a global meteorological data system to provide real time weather for all locations present in the game - that means that if you select the current date and hour for a race at Silverstone and it´s currently raining there, you´ll get the same weather in AMS2; if it has just stopped raining a couple of hours earlier, the track will still be wet in real life, and it will likewise still be wet in AMS2 as well. Real Weather does not just mimic current weather conditions though - it packs data for every single day over the last 40 years for every track in the game, allowing users to reproduce historical races in changeable weather very closely to how they actually happened.<h2 class="bb_tag">MOTORSPORTS RULES &amp; REGULATIONS </h2>- Automobilista 2 also features one of the most complete sets of rules &amp; regulations of any racing sim, allowing users to emulate rules of most major series in the world. In V1.4 we expand that reach with the introduction of oval racing and the support for Full Course Yellow. AM2 also allows users to customize multiclass races with the exact number of opponents from each class they may desire.<h2 class="bb_tag">RACING LEGENDS</h2>A growing library of famous historical racing cars and race tracks as they were through various decades offer players the opportunity to relive classic eras of motorsports history<h2 class="bb_tag">EVER EVOLVING, EVER EXPANDING</h2>Boasting a commitment to a long-term development cycle, Automobilista 2 receives regular monthly game updates bringing in a constant flow of new features and improvements to the game along with new cars and tracks						</div>
					</div><div class="game_page_autocollapse_fade"><div class="game_page_autocollapse_readmore">展开阅读</div></div></div>

	<div data-panel="{&quot;type&quot;:&quot;PanelGroup&quot;}" class="review_box    partial">
		<div id="ReviewContentsummary66316972">

								<a href="https://steamcommunity.com/id/lolikawaiiyukari/recommended/1066890/" class="vote_header tooltip" data-tooltip-text="阅读完整评测">
					<div class="thumb">

										<img class="review_source tooltip" data-tooltip-text="产品是从 Steam 直接购买的" src="https://store.akamai.steamstatic.com/public/shared/images/userreviews/icon_review_steam.png">
					
					<div class="title ellipsis">推荐</div>
										<div class="hours ellipsis">
						总时数 102.1 小时												（评测时 2.0 小时）											</div>

													<div class="responsive_review_leftcol_ctn" id="ReviewContentsummary66316972_leftcol_ctn"></div>
				
				<div class="postedDate">
					发布于：2020 年 4 月 1 日																					<div class="responsive_purchase_source">
															Steam 直接购买													</div>
									</div>

								
				<div class="content">
					v1.2了，AMS2是个好游戏吗？- 更新评测原因：物理大更新<br><br>我曾经分别在EA阶段和V1.0阶段写下了评测，并且都是谨慎乐观的态度。可能我在v1.0的时候还是有些高估他们的进展了，Reiza工作室现在因为巴西的疫情，开发效率下降不少。<br><br>Reiza在之前三个月的时间里几乎没有新内容推出，然后他们就在V1.2导入了一大堆新东西，USA Pack1也在同一时间发布了。工作室还是那个小工作室，开发进度可能也就比RF2好一些，一些功能性的目标也可能在后面几个季度内才能实现，不过这并不妨碍体验这款游戏。还是不支持中文，我也在一直关心这件事看看Reiza会不会哪天找人翻中文。<br><br>游戏现在新增了过去40年的天气数据，并且支持从OpenWeather获取实时天气，而且有意思的是它会回溯比赛日期时间之前几小时的天气并模拟赛道状况。如果赛前几小时下雨了，那就真的会是湿地开始。谁不想跑跑风雨交加的2019 WEC斯帕呢？当然了，我这么说是因为GTE赛车的加入。如果你更喜欢IMSA的比赛那么现在也有了DPi可选择。游戏现在也支持了橡胶堆积并能预设堆积程度。联机实时天气7月上线。<br><br>Madness引擎的游戏似乎确实有一款车一个样的问题，不过整体的操控感受在V1.2确实有了一个大更新，很多人，包括之前狂吹AMS2但是实在吹不动决定不再玩的Ermin吹神，都对V1.2有了一个积极的评价（噗…）。物理方面，车辆的疯狂甩尾的问题被大大减轻了，所有车辆都感觉更加稳健，除了一些功能上的，比如差速器和快速阻尼之类的问题还需要调整，就看这些破轮胎能不能做好了。SMS你看看你到底挖了多大坑…因为这游戏胎压和胎温因为环境会改变所以每个弯都不一样所以还没法直接跟别的游戏比…<br><br>除了此前推荐的那些车，游戏目前手感最好的是加入的三台GTE，特别是保时捷RSR，其在声音方面也是非常不错。赛道方面，银石、斯帕、纽伯格林、以及长滩、戴通纳、拉古纳塞卡现在都已经做进了游戏。大部分赛道看起来都很像PC2中的，但其实Reiza以及重新修改了各种路面以及物体细节。现在各条赛道的景色更以四季不同的形式呈现。<br><br>FFB在V1.2之前又有过几次调整，现在基本上算最终版本？实在不喜欢的那就去论坛扒Silver Raw的rFuktor吧，挺多人用了就不想再用游戏内置的了。<br><br>AI呢？我之前说了那么多单其实AI还是抖抖抖个不停的。在V1.2，AI变得超级好，现在在大多数情况不会把你晃瞎也不会抖个不停。唯一问题可能还是你能不能追上的问题。<br><br>那么又到了值不值得买的环节。AMS2现在的问题已经说是修好了很多，不过多设备支持、联机功能的缺失、各种小问题导致它还有挺长一段路要走。不过，作为日常娱乐并且获得快乐的一种手段，那V1.2版本对你来说可能已经足够了。后面Reiza还会带来USA包的Part2和Part3，分别对应IndyCar和NASCAR。2022年往后呢？那我就不知道了，Reiza一直会支持到2025年以后的。<br><br>---------分隔线----------<br><br>下方评测基于v1.0。<br><br>在2020年的4月1日，Beta版发售的第一天，我就在steam评价了这款游戏。相比赛车计划2，AMS2确实很好。但是够好吗？这倒有些复杂了。这是我当时写下的原话：<br><br>“AMS 2依然是在改进。ACC的第一个EA版本，一车一赛道，说未来会有光追，还没有联机，非常简陋。给Reiza点时间，多上Reiza论坛唠叨吧。”<br><br>这句话看起来只是一个比较“谨慎乐观”的态度，一方面是0.8.4版本时的AMS2，物理和FFB存在很多问题，另一方面很多人认为Reiza只是个小作坊，没有能力去驾驭Madness Engine，认为最终AMS2仍然会有明显的赛车计划2特性。不过最终，虽然晚了6个月，AMS2的版本号终于来到了v1.0。游戏尚未支持中文，不过v1.0的完成度对于这个二十几号人的小工作室而言应该开发速度已经到了极限吧，既然开发路线图里写了，那么后面应该会加上的。<br><br>游戏画面风格和界面结果一眼便知是赛车计划2的引擎，当然会支持Live Track 3.0。不过UI是Reiza自己设计的，赛道也是Reiza自己建好的。三屏、VR的支持也延续了过来。除此以外，这款游戏和赛车计划2的关系也就止步于此了。<br><br>车辆方面，v1.0相比Beta的最后一版新加入了三台80年代的F1真车，Ginetta的G55 GT4和G58 LMP3（巴西耐力锦标赛P1组），StockCar 2020两台车，还有2018款科迈罗SS。至于那些你不认识的车，他们都是80年代的巴西赛车，都是真实的车辆，可以开一开哦。<br><br>在V1.0游戏里能拥有一台Ginetta G55真是极好的，这款车能够非常容易地接近极限，所以你能和赛车计划2的同款车和ACC未来将会发售的GT4系列同款车进行对比，这样你就能更好地了解这款游戏的物理引擎到底有什么能力。我强烈建议体验一下Ginetta G55 GT4这款车，操控起来非常顺滑，没有赛车计划2神奇滑动的影子。<br><br>其它推荐体验的车型包括卡特汉姆Superlight（360R）、Sigma P1、Poco 001、SprintRace、任意时代的假F1、Ultma GTR Race、各款卡丁车。未来半年这款游戏已经确认会增加的内容还有90年代DTM、以及巴西GT3、GT4组别的赛车，他们都是本体的内容。其它的车，一些车我不喜欢，还有一些车处于尚未打磨完成的状态，需要等待以后优化。<br><br>赛道方面，就如宣传片可见，除了游戏内目前的内容之外，在未来半年内还将有银石、斯帕、纽伯格林北环等赛道。奥山在v1.0赶工了出来，很多布景还没有完成。当然了，除了奥山一位，很多赛道即使在赛车计划2出现过，在AMS2中依然重新建了摸，这其中当然包括Brands Hatch和多宁顿公园。担心黑洞路肩的同学可以放心了，想往路肩上Push的同学可以尽情Push，当然赛道边界系统Reiza还是给沿用了下来，不过正赛不再需要你那样激进地减速了。<br><br>不过，可能上面这些内容你都不关心，你关心的是物理和FFB。AMS2的物理和FFB是一点一点进步的，FFB在0.9.7终于达到了一个可以说是完工了的状态，可以在设置按键后开箱即用。如果你对0.8.4时的驾驶感觉不满意，现在可以再次尝试了。但是切记，如果你是从之前的版本升级上来，请务必删掉我的文档内的存档并重新设置整个游戏，不然FFB会100%工作不正常。L家、T家方向盘记得使用校准，F家方向盘记得方向盘度数使用AUTO。<br><br>物理的改动即使到v1.0也依然没有停。现在，这款游戏真正拥有了感受重心转移的能力，最明显的一个例子就是循迹刹车入弯，在松开刹车时车身会有稍微的转向不足出现。滑动时的情况也是如此，在0.8.4车身滑移时你会有一种轮胎绷着劲，随时可能结束滑动的感觉，现在滑动就非常自然了。对于刹车容易锁死的问题，Reiza在这几个版本一直在改善刹车，现在的刹车系统可能需要自己调调力度，但是一般都能正常踩下去了。最大的也是唯一的问题是极限滑得有点突然，官方说会进一步优化轮胎。<br><br>蹭墙掉速、雨刷、现在也都已经修好了。AI应该仍然有一些问题，不过这已经比0.8.4好太多了，后面还会改。赛道边的广告牌也不再只有Reiza和AMS2了。联机方面一路下来进老外局也没什么大问题。DRS和尾翼动画、KERS现在也已经运作正常。					<div class="gradient"></div>
				</div>

						总时数 211.8 小时												（评测时 20.9 小时）											</div>
									</a>
				
				
													<div class="responsive_review_leftcol_ctn" id="ReviewContentsummary91660549_leftcol_ctn"></div>
				
				<div class="postedDate">
					发布于：2021 年 5 月 9 日																					<div class="responsive_purchase_source">
															Steam 直接购买													</div>
									</div>

								
				<div class="content">
					开了两个星期了，这期间不断地在rF2，AC，AMS2，F1 2020之间切换，AMS2我觉得对于开轮赛车爱好者绝对是一个必买项，各种时代的F1赛车应有尽有，质量也不是第三方MOD可以轻易超过的，比如Formula U 2019，可以较为近似的模拟近年的F1赛车，在银石赛道，全油门时间，大直道挡位都和F1 2020还有真实录像差不多，当然力回馈手感完爆F1 2020，反而很多人夸赞的RSS MOD组制作的AC RSS Formula Hybrid 2021感觉和当前F1不太匹配，银石两个大直道竟然是勉勉强强升到8档，而且RSS的mod 齿比是固定的，虽然现实F1的齿比近年也都是锁死的，但是RSS提供的默认齿比明显让我感到很难复制现实车手的操作。<br>AMS2的手感我个人觉得是ac和rf2类型的融合，以GT3赛车为例，在车身重量转移方面，力回馈给出的信息很像AC，重量转移对比明显，不想rF2那么”线性“。AMS2过弯时可以带一点滑动，至少是你可以感觉出的滑动，跟rF2比较相像。Youtube上很多人说AMS2 slip everywhere，可能早期版本是如此，现在的版本我觉得rear绝对没有rF2那么活跃。不至于像rF2一样到处滑着走，但是也不是AC那样一瞬间失控，后轮打滑的感觉较为清晰。但是感觉力回馈稍微有点滞后。不像rF2那么sharp。如果说你认为rF2依然是sim king，我觉得AMS2在轮胎的滑动这一点上绝对算不上差（反正现实我没开过赛车）。AC在这一点上表现很差，包括ACC也不怎么样。力回馈给出的信息是我知道重量已经转移到侧后方，但是就是不知道轮胎是否已经开始打滑，轮胎一开始打滑，抓地力就掉悬崖，中间的过渡段非常模糊而且变化非常快。我开始觉得这是轮胎抽象模型本质的差别，我在店里试过ACC，ACC的oversteer风格还是非常的Kunos。重量转移应该是悬挂模型造成的效果，一般赛车轮胎在这方面作用感觉不强。但是方程式赛车的震动很大一部分由轮胎吸收，这个时候轮胎模型的重要性就凸显出来了。然而无论AC还是ACC的五点式tyre model，都过于简化，虽然准确的悬挂模型依然提供了优秀的力回馈手感，但是那种轮胎橡胶变形，与地面同时滚动加滑动的信息体现不出来，手感过于的硬。madness的SETA轮胎模型和rF2相像，都采用了类似有限元的方法模拟轮胎形变。AMS2的方程式手感非常类似rF2，用大头的understeer驾驶方法，高速弯狠扔方向，赛车稍微失去后部，然后在下压力作用下，很快转变为转向不足的感觉跟rF2不能说一模一样，只能说完全一致。抓地力变化通过细微的FFB变化清晰反馈给你。只能说一个字，爽！<br>不太爽的地方是UI偶尔会遇到小bug，PC2遗毒之类的，有些设置没有解释信息，google了半天才搞明白。还有就是路肩感觉太安全了，抓地力有点足，，即使是大雨天，好像上路肩也没有什么严重的后果，甚至有一种更稳的感觉，难道是因为路肩高上边水少。。。有现实车手这么干吗。。。这一点感觉比AC和rF2都差。					<div class="gradient"></div>
				</div>

									<div class="early_access_review tooltip" data-tooltip-text="该评测被撰写时，Automobilista 2 被标记为 Steam 抢先体验游戏">抢先体验版本评测</div>
				
													<div class="responsive_review_leftcol_ctn" id="ReviewContentsummary67001637_leftcol_ctn"></div>
				
				<div class="postedDate">
					发布于：2020 年 4 月 10 日																					<div class="responsive_purchase_source">
															Steam 直接购买													</div>
									</div>

								
				<div class="content">
					总结: 现在不建议已经有其他赛车模拟软件的玩家购买. ACC, RF2, iRacing这三款要比现阶段的AMS2优秀. 没有这3款的玩家, 推荐购买AMS2, 等打折的时候入RF2. AMS2未来有潜力超过ACC, 达到RF2和iRacing级别. <br><br>画面和可玩性, AMS2作为游戏足够好玩. 物理真实性和FFB已经很好了, 稍逊于RF2. 需要改进碰撞物理, 减少bug. 官方已经计划完善在线排位系统, 期待发展成可以对标iRacing的赛车游戏平台. <br><br>+ 画面: 9/10 达到了ACC水准<br>+ 流畅: 9/10 帧数比较高, 全最高画质 &gt;110FPS@5700xt+ryzen 1700+16G<br>+ FFB: 8/10 手感反馈的响应速度快, 细节较多. 希望可以增加调整选项, 便于调整手感. <br>+ 内容: 8/10 组别多, 对我足够了<br><br>- 完成度: 6/10 bug还是比较多<br>- 物理: 7/10 , 碰撞物理做的不好. seta轮胎模型和rfactor 2对比网格划分不够细, 轮胎形变确实模拟了, 但是比RF2稍微差一点. 如果碰撞改好可以达到9分(RF2是10分的话)<br><br>预期(碰撞改动后会改为推荐) <br>FFB: 9/10 增加调节选项, 也许会达到RF2的水准<br>画面: 9/10 已经很好, 减少bug就可以<br>流畅: 9/10 已经很好, 三屏和VR都容易达到高帧数, 目前最好<br>物理: 9/10 轮胎模型不会达到RF2水准(主要是弹性的细腻程度和碰撞), 未来大概率可以达到或超过ACC. 除了RF2, 应该是Tire 1<br>内容: 8/10  我觉得挺丰富, 没必要买季票					<div class="gradient"></div>
				</div>

															Steam 直接购买													</div>
									</div>

								
				<div class="content">
					现在的手感确实比以前的要好了，abs的逻辑比原来强太多了，可惜的就是车，我觉得车太少了，gt3什么的就几辆，但是种类多。没有中文确实是一个缺点，但是不太影响。总的来说，这个sim路面信息反馈丰富，能明显感觉出轮胎的橡胶感。车损做的比较糊弄，我觉得没有project car2做的好，回火的动画比较尴尬。手感没毛病，希望能一直更新下去。加油。Vamos					<div class="gradient"></div>
